import torch
import torch.nn as nn

class Model(nn.Module):
    """
    Simple model that performs Max Pooling 3D.
    """
    def __init__(self, kernel_size: int, stride: int = None, padding: int = 0, dilation: int = 1, return_indices: bool = False, ceil_mode: bool = False):
        """
        Initializes the Max Pooling 3D layer.

        Args:
            kernel_size (int): Size of the kernel for the max pooling operation.
            stride (int, optional): Stride of the pooling operation. Defaults to None, which means stride is equal to kernel_size.
            padding (int, optional): Padding applied to the input tensor. Defaults to 0.
            dilation (int, optional): Spacing between kernel elements. Defaults to 1.
            return_indices (bool, optional): Whether to return indices of the maximum values. Defaults to False.
            ceil_mode (bool, optional): When True, the output size is ceil(input_size / stride) instead of floor. Defaults to False.
        """
        super(Model, self).__init__()
        self.maxpool = nn.MaxPool3d(kernel_size=kernel_size, stride=stride, padding=padding, dilation=dilation, return_indices=return_indices, ceil_mode=ceil_mode)

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Applies Max Pooling 3D to the input tensor.

        Args:
            x (torch.Tensor): Input tensor of shape (batch_size, channels, dim1, dim2, dim3).

        Returns:
            torch.Tensor: Output tensor with Max Pooling 3D applied.
        """
        return self.maxpool(x)

batch_size = 16
channels = 32
dim1 = 128
dim2 = 128
dim3 = 128
kernel_size = 3
stride = 2
padding = 1
dilation = 3

def get_inputs():
    x = torch.rand(batch_size, channels, dim1, dim2, dim3)
    return [x]

def get_init_inputs():
    return [kernel_size, stride, padding, dilation]

Kernel: __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW, int KD, int KH, int KW, int SD, int SH, int SW, int PD, int PH, int PW, int DD, int DH, int DW) { int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y; // decode n, c, od from blockIdx.z int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return; const float* in_ptr = input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * ID * IH * IW; // float maxval = -CUDART_INF_F; float maxval = -1e30f; // Unroll loops manually? Use #pragma unroll if possible. for (int kd = 0; kd < KD; ++kd) { int id = od * SD + kd * DD - PD; if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue; for (int kh = 0; kh < KH; ++kh) { int ih = oh * SH + kh * DH - PH; if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue; for (int kw = 0; kw < KW; ++kw) { int iw = ow * SW + kw * DW - PW; if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue; float val = in_ptr[((size_t)id * IH + ih) * IW + iw]; if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } size_t out_idx = (((size_t)blockIdx.z * OD + od) * OH + oh) * OW + ow; // Wait blockIdx.z already encodes n,c,od. Let's derive output index simpler. // Actually blockIdx.z = ((n*C)+c)*OD + od. // So output index = ((size_t)blockIdx.z * OH + oh) * OW + ow. output[((size_t)blockIdx.z * OH + oh) * OW + ow] = maxval; } Yes, output slice per (n,c,od) is contiguous with size OH*OW. So index = blockIdx.z * OH * OW + oh * OW + ow. Thus: size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW; output[out_offset + oh * OW + ow] = maxval; We need to compute oh*OW+ow which is small. However, since each thread only reads 27 values and reuse is modest (some input elements reused across output threads in same block), the benefit may be small. For example, a block of 64 threads processes 64 outputs. Input footprint size ≈ 3*21*21 = 1323 floats. Total unique loads = 1323. With direct global loads, 64 threads * 27 loads = 1728 loads. So shared memory reduces global loads by about 24% (since some loads are shared among threads). Not huge. Plus the overhead of loading and synchronizing. Maybe not worth it. But more importantly, direct loads may benefit from L1 cache (which caches global loads automatically). The footprint of 3x21x21 floats per block is ~5KB, which likely fits in L1. Since threads in same block access similar input region, L1 cache will capture reuse automatically. So a custom shared memory tile may not be much better than relying on L1/L2 cache. torch::Tensor maxpool3d_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor input, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, bool return_indices, bool ceil_mode) { // Ensure input is contiguous and on CUDA auto x = input.contiguous(); int N = x.size(0); int C = x.size(1); int ID = x.size(2); int IH = x.size(3); int IW = x.size(4); int K = kernel_size; int S = stride; if (S <= 0) S = K; // default stride = kernel_size int P = padding; int D = dilation; auto compute_out_size = [&](int64_t in_size) -> int64_t { int64_t num = in_size + 2 * P - D * (K - 1) - 1; if (ceil_mode) { return (num + S - 1) / S + 1; } else { return num / S + 1; } }; int64_t OD = compute_out_size(ID); int64_t OH = compute_out_size(IH); int64_t OW = compute_out_size(IW); // Handle negative output size (too much padding) by clamping to 0? PyTorch would raise. if (OD <= 0 || OH <= 0 || OW <= 0) { // Return empty tensor similar to PyTorch auto out = torch::empty({N, C, std::max<int64_t>(OD,0), std::max<int64_t>(OH,0), std::max<int64_t>(OW,0)}, x.options()); idx_ptr = indices.data_ptr<int64_t>(); } if (output.numel() == 0) { if (return_indices) { return std::make_tuple(output, indices); } else { return output; } } const int BX = 32; const int BY = 8; dim3 block(BX, BY, 1); Actually PyTorch docs: `ceil_mode=True` means using ceil instead of floor. There is also that some last windows that start in the right padding are dropped if they would have no valid elements? Let's check: In PyTorch source, max_pool output size formula is: ``` auto output_size = (input_size + 2 * pad - dilation * (kernel_size - 1) - 1 + (ceil_mode ? stride - 1 : 0)) / stride + 1; ``` Yes, that's equivalent to our formula: - floor: (num) / stride + 1 - ceil: (num + stride - 1) / stride + 1 Provided num >=0. If num <0, the formula may give 0 or negative? In PyTorch they clamp to at least 1? Actually they might throw error if the resulting size <=0. Let's just replicate the formula. Let's define: ``` int64_t out_size = (in + 2*P - D*(K-1) - 1 + (ceil_mode ? S-1 : 0)) / S + 1; ``` This matches the C++ code in ATen. Edge case: if numerator is negative and ceil_mode is True, adding S-1 might still be negative, integer division truncates toward zero in C++ (but numerator is negative?). However, since inputs are large, not an issue. So our `compute_out_size` should be: ``` int64_t num = in_size + 2 * P - D * (K - 1) - 1; int64_t out_size = (num + (ceil_mode ? S - 1 : 0)) / S + 1; ``` Let's verify with our numbers: ID=128, P=1, D=3, K=3, S=2, ceil=False. num = 128 + 2 - 3*2 -1 = 128+2-6-1=123. out = 123/2 +1 = 61 +1 =62. Good. Let's implement that. Let's implement template version: ```cpp template <int KD, int KH, int KW> __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_tmpl( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int64_t* __restrict__ indices, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW, int SD, int SH, int SW, int PD, int PH, int PW, int DD, int DH, int DW) { int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y; int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return; size_t plane = (size_t)ID * IH * IW; size_t row = (size_t)IH * IW; if (all_inside) { #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; kd < KD; ++kd) { size_t off_d = (size_t)(id0 + kd * DD) * row; #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < KH; ++kh) { size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)(ih0 + kh * DH) * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < KW; ++kw) { float val = in_ptr[off_h + iw0 + kw * DW]; if (val > maxval) { maxval = val; maxidx = off_h + iw0 + kw * DW; } } } } } else { #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; kd < KD; ++kd) { int id = id0 + kd * DD; if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue; size_t off_d = (size_t)id * row; #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < KH; ++kh) { int ih = ih0 + kh * DH; if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue; size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)ih * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < KW; ++kw) { int iw = iw0 + kw * DW; if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue; float val = in_ptr[off_h + iw]; if (val > maxval) { maxval = val; This is okay. Another thing: `blockIdx.z` dimension is `N*C*OD = 31,744`. With `grid.z` = 31,744, we have 31,744 blocks in z. That's okay. But block size is BX=32, BY=8. S - 1 : 0)) / S + 1; }; int OD = compute_out_size(ID); int OH = compute_out_size(IH); int OW = compute_out_size(IW); if (OD <= 0 || OH <= 0 || OW <= 0) { return torch::empty({N, C, std::max<int64_t>(OD, 0), std::max<int64_t>(OH, 0), std::max<int64_t>(OW, 0)}, x.options()); } auto output = torch::empty({N, C, OD, OH, OW}, x.options()); // ... launch kernel return output; } ``` One issue: `std::max<int64_t>` - need `<algorithm>`? `torch/extension.h` probably includes it. Actually, we can branch at the block or grid level: process all pixels with a generic kernel, or even just process them all with the same code. The branch is: ```cpp if (id0 >= 0 && ih0 >= 0 && iw0 >= 0) { // unrolled no-bounds-check loop } else { // unrolled bounds-check loop } ``` Since only the planes at 0 need the else branch, warps where od>0, oh>0, ow>0 all take the if-branch. The proportion of threads in a block that might take the else branch depends on how we organize. If we put od in blockIdx.z, then entire blocks are either at od=0 or od>0. So blocks with od>0 take entirely the fast path. This is perfect. Similarly for oh and ow: oh=0 only for the first row of blocks in y, and ow=0 for the first column of blocks in x. So most blocks are entirely in the fast path. Let's use this design. Kernel: ```cpp __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_special( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW) { int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y; int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return; int id0 = od * 2 - 1; int ih0 = oh * 2 - 1; int iw0 = ow * 2 - 1; const float* in_ptr = input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * ID * IH * IW; float maxval = -FLT_MAX; if (id0 >= 0 && ih0 >= 0 && iw0 >= 0) { // Fast path: all accesses in bounds // Note: we also need to ensure id0 + 6 < ID. But ID=128, id0 max=121, 121+6=127 < 128. So always true. // Same for ih and iw. #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; kd < 3; ++kd) { size_t off_d = (size_t)(id0 + kd * 3) * IH * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < 3; ++kh) { size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)(ih0 + kh * 3) * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < 3; ++kw) { float val = in_ptr[off_h + iw0 + kw * 3]; if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } } else { // Slow path: some accesses out of bounds // Only possible for id0=-1, ih0=-1, or iw0=-1. #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; kd < 3; ++kd) { int id = id0 + kd * 3; if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue; size_t off_d = (size_t)id * IH * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < 3; ++kh) { int ih = ih0 + kh * 3; if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue; size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)ih * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < 3; ++kw) { int iw = iw0 + kw * 3; if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue; float val = in_ptr[off_h + iw]; if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } } size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow; output[out_offset] = maxval; } ``` This kernel is fully unrolled in the inner loop (27 iterations). It uses constant propagation for strides, padding, dilation. But is this enough to beat PyTorch? Maybe. PyTorch's kernel might have dynamic loop bounds and more complex indexing. Let's also consider using vectorized loads. Since dilation=3, adjacent memory accesses in the inner loop are separated by 3 floats. But within a warp, threads access `iw0 + kw*3`, where `iw0` differs by 2 between threads. Wait, thread `t` accesses `in_ptr[... + (iw0_t) + kw*3]`. `iw0_t = (blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + t) * 2 - 1`. So adjacent threads in x access memory at offset `... + (2*t)*2 -1 + kw*3 = ... + 4*t -1 + kw*3`. Wait, `iw0` differs by 2 between consecutive threads? Actually `ow` differs by 1, `iw0 = ow*2 - 1`, so `iw0` differs by 2. Then `iw0 + kw*3` for a fixed `kw`: difference between threads is 2 floats. So memory accesses are coalesced but with a stride of 2. This means each warp request loads 32 * 2 * 4 = 256 bytes, but with 2x waste because of stride? Actually, global memory loads are done per-cache-line (128 bytes). If each thread loads a 4-byte float at addresses `a, a+8, a+16, ...`, the warp accesses a range of `a` to `a+8*31 = a+248`. This spans 2 or 3 cache lines. Each thread's request is spaced by 8 bytes. So 50% of each cache line is useful. So memory bandwidth utilization is ~50% for coalesced but strided loads. This is not great. If we could reorganize to compute 2 output pixels per thread in the W dimension, then the threads in the warp would access addresses with stride 4? No. If thread computes ow and ow+1, then its accesses are at iw0 and iw0+2. The two loads are close. But across the warp, we'd have half the threads. Can we reorder threads to access contiguous memory? For example, instead of mapping threads to output pixels, map them to input pixels? Or use a thread to compute output from a contiguous chunk of input W? Output `ow` depends on input windows starting at `iw0 = 2*ow-1` (with stride 2). The window accesses `iw0`, `iw0+3`, `iw0+6`. These are not contiguous. But we can have threads process multiple `kw` values simultaneously? Or use float4? Since loads are separated by 3, we can't easily use vectorized types for the inner `kw` loop. But across the warp, we have 32 threads loading 32 floats that are strided by 2. This is suboptimal but not terrible (50% utilization of L2/cache lines). If we group threads such that they process every other output pixel? Not helpful. Can we do better? Use shared memory as a staging area: Load a contiguous chunk of input W (e.g., 64 or 128 floats) into shared memory, then threads read from shared memory with stride. Shared memory can handle arbitrary strides with no bandwidth penalty (as long as no bank conflicts). Bank conflicts: shared memory is banked by 4 bytes. Access pattern: thread t loads shared_mem[idx_t]. idx_t differs by 2 between threads. This causes 2-way bank conflicts (since stride 2 means threads 0 and 16 share bank, 1 and 17, etc.). This halves effective shared memory bandwidth. Still better than global memory strided loads? Global memory with stride 2 has 50% utilization due to cache line waste. Shared memory with 2-way bank conflict also has 50% throughput. Not a huge win. But shared memory allows us to load global memory with coalesced contiguous pattern (100% utilization), then read with bank conflicts. Is the overhead of loading shared memory worth it? Global memory traffic: for a block of 32x8 threads (256 outputs), input footprint is W: 32*2+6=70, H: 8*2+6=22, D: 8. Total unique loads = 8*22*70 = 12320. With global direct: 256*27=6912 loads (but half cache line utilization). Wait, earlier I said 256*27=6912. But the unique footprint is 12320, which is larger because of no overlap. So the direct kernel loads 6912 floats per block. Unique footprint is actually 12320, meaning some loads are shared across threads? No, because we established windows are disjoint for adjacent outputs. So total unique loads for 256 outputs should be 256 * 27 = 6912. Why did I get 12320? Because I computed bounding box W=70, H=22, D=8. 70*22*8=12320. But the actual accessed points are sparse. Since dilation=3 and kernel=3, each window has 3 points in W separated by 3. 32 windows side by side (W) cover 32*3 = 96 points, but with stride 2, the windows are interleaved. Similarly in H and D. Therefore, for a 2D tile of 32x8 threads, total unique accesses = 32 * 8 * 3 * 3 * 3 = 6912. Exactly 256 * 27. So there is literally zero reuse between threads. My bounding box calculation was misleading. This is crucial: there is no data reuse. So shared memory provides no benefit for reducing global memory bandwidth. Actually, in a warp, thread t loads `in_ptr[base + 2t -1]`, `in_ptr[base + 2t + 2]`, etc. The first load: addresses `base-1, base+1, base+3, ...`. These are strided by 2. Implementation plan: **cpp_sources:** ```cpp #include <torch/extension.h> torch::Tensor maxpool3d_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor input, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, bool ceil_mode); ``` **cuda_sources:** ```cu #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cfloat> #include <torch/extension.h> // Generic kernel __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_generic_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW, int K, int S, int P, int D) { int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y; int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return; int id0 = od * S - P; int ih0 = oh * S - P; int iw0 = ow * S - P; size_t plane = (size_t)ID * IH * IW; const float* in_ptr = input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * plane; float maxval = -FLT_MAX; #pragma unroll 1 for (int kd = 0; kd < K; ++kd) { int id = id0 + kd * D; if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue; size_t off_d = (size_t)id * IH * IW; #pragma unroll 1 for (int kh = 0; kh < K; ++kh) { int ih = ih0 + kh * D; if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue; size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)ih * IW; #pragma unroll 1 for (int kw = 0; kw < K; ++kw) { int iw = iw0 + kw * D; if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue; float val = __ldg(in_ptr + off_h + iw); if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow; output[out_offset] = maxval; } // Specialized kernel for K=3, S=2, P=1, D=3 (ceil_mode=False) __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_k3s2p1d3_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW) { int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y; int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return; const size_t plane = (size_t)ID * IH * IW; const float* in_ptr = input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * plane; int id0 = od * 2 - 1; int ih0 = oh * 2 - 1; int iw0 = ow * 2 - 1; float maxval = -FLT_MAX; bool fast = (id0 >= 0 && ih0 >= 0 && iw0 >= 0); if (fast) { #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; kd < 3; ++kd) { size_t off_d = (size_t)(id0 + kd * 3) * IH * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < 3; ++kh) { size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)(ih0 + kh * 3) * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < 3; ++kw) { float val = __ldg(in_ptr + off_h + iw0 + kw * 3); if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } } else { #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; kd < 3; ++kd) { int id = id0 + kd * 3; if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue; size_t off_d = (size_t)id * IH * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < 3; ++kh) { int ih = ih0 + kh * 3; if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue; size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)ih * IW; #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < 3; ++kw) { int iw = iw0 + kw * 3; if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue; float val = __ldg(in_ptr + off_h + iw); if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } } size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow; output[out_offset] = maxval; } torch::Tensor maxpool3d_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor input, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, bool ceil_mode) { auto x = input.contiguous(); int N = x.size(0); int C = x.size(1); int ID = x.size(2); int IH = x.size(3); int IW = x.size(4); int K = kernel_size; int S = stride; if (S <= 0) S = K; int P = padding; int D = dilation; auto compute_out_size = [&](int64_t in_size) -> int64_t { int64_t num = in_size + 2 * P - D * (K - 1) - 1; return (num + (ceil_mode ? S - 1 : 0)) / S + 1; }; int64_t OD = compute_out_size(ID); int64_t OH = compute_out_size(IH); int64_t OW = compute_out_size(IW); if (OD <= 0 || OH <= 0 || OW <= 0) { return torch::empty({N, C, std::max<int64_t>(OD, 0), std::max<int64_t>(OH, 0), std::max<int64_t>(OW, 0)}, x.options()); } auto output = torch::empty({N, C, OD, OH, OW}, x.options()); const int BX = 32; const int BY = 8; dim3 block(BX, BY, 1); dim3 grid( (OW + BX - 1) / BX, (OH + BY - 1) / BY, N * C * OD ); bool is_specialized = (K == 3 && S == 2 && P == 1 && D == 3 && !ceil_mode); if (is_specialized) { maxpool3d_forward_k3s2p1d3_kernel<<<grid, block>>>( x.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), N, C, ID, IH, IW, OD, OH, OW ); } else { maxpool3d_forward_generic_kernel<<<grid, block>>>( x.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), N, C, ID, IH, IW, OD, OH, OW, K, S, P, D ); } C10_CUDA_KERNEL_LAUNCH_CHECK(); return output; } ``` Wait, `C10_CUDA_KERNEL_LAUNCH_CHECK()` is a macro from PyTorch. It checks `cudaGetLastError()`. But can we use it in the `.cu` file? It should be available via `<torch/extension.h>`. Also, `std::max<int64_t>` requires `<algorithm>`, but likely included. In `cpp_sources`, we don't need much. We should also import `torch.nn.functional as F` in Python for fallback. For `return_indices`, our CUDA function just returns a Tensor. In `ModelNew.forward()`: ```python if self.return_indices: return F.max_pool3d_with_indices(x, self.kernel_size, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, self.ceil_mode) else: return _maxpool3d_ext.maxpool3d_forward_cuda(x, ...) ``` Actually, `F.max_pool3d(input, kernel_size, stride, padding, dilation, return_indices=False, ceil_mode=False)` returns a Tensor or a tuple. `F.max_pool3d_with_indices` returns tuple. But we can do: ```python if self.return_indices: out, indices = torch.nn.functional.max_pool3d_with_indices( x, self.kernel_size, self.stride, self.padding, self.dilation, self.ceil_mode ) return out, indices return _maxpool3d_ext.maxpool3d_forward_cuda(...) ``` But the reference returns just a Tensor when `return_indices=False`, which is our case. Wait, the signature of `forward` is `def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:`. It returns a single Tensor. The harness probably checks `out = model(x)` and compares. It won't use `return_indices`. So we can ignore `return_indices` in the fast path, but for compatibility with constructor signature, we should handle it. Now, let's think about correctness. The output size computation must match PyTorch exactly. Our `compute_out_size`: `num = in_size + 2 * P - D * (K - 1) - 1`. For `in_size=128, P=1, D=3, K=3`: `num = 128 + 2 - 3*2 - 1 = 130 - 6 - 1 = 123`. If `ceil_mode=False`: `out_size = num / S + 1 = 123 / 2 + 1 = 61 + 1 = 62`. PyTorch formula for `ceil_mode=False`: `floor((L + 2*padding - dilation*(kernel_size-1) - 1) / stride) + 1`. Yes, integer division floor. If `ceil_mode=True`: `(num + S - 1) / S + 1`. For 123: `(123 + 1)/2 + 1 = 124/2 + 1 = 62 + 1 = 63`. PyTorch: `ceil((L + 2*padding - dilation*(kernel_size-1) - 1) / stride) + 1`. For 123/2=61.5, ceil=62, +1 = 63. Correct. So size computation is correct. Bounds checking: for `fast` path in specialized kernel, we check `id0 >= 0 && ih0 >= 0 && iw0 >= 0`. We also need to ensure upper bounds are valid, but as we reasoned, for the given config they always are. This is safe only when we know `id0 + (K-1)*D < ID`. Let's verify: `id0` max is `od_max * 2 - 1`. `od_max = OD-1 = 61`. `id0 = 121`. `121 + 6 = 127 < 128 = ID`. Yes. So always safe. But what if the user passes different sizes? We only use `is_specialized` when `ID, IH, IW` are exactly 128 (or smaller, but OD/OH/OW are computed based on ID). Wait, `is_specialized` only checks K, S, P, D, ceil_mode; it doesn't check ID/IH/IW. For other ID values, `id0 + 6` might exceed `ID`. Example: `ID=4`. `P=1, K=3, S=2, D=3`. `OD = floor((4+2-6-1)/2)+1 = floor(-1/2)+1 = -1+1? Wait floor(-0.5) = -1. So OD=0. numel=0. So no kernel launched. Example: `ID=10`. `OD = floor((10+2-6-1)/2)+1 = floor(5/2)+1 = 2+1=3`. `od=2`: `id0=3`. `3+6=9 < 10`. OK. But is it always true for P=1, K=3, D=3, S=2? Let's see. For any `ID`, the last output `od = OD-1`. `id0 = (OD-1)*2 - 1`. We need `(OD-1)*2 - 1 + 6 <= ID-1`, i.e., `(OD-1)*2 + 5 <= ID-1`, i.e., `2*OD + 3 <= ID`. What is `OD`? `OD = floor((ID + 2 - 6 - 1)/2) + 1 = floor((ID - 5)/2) + 1`. If `ID` is even: `ID=2m`. `OD = floor((2m-5)/2)+1 = m-3 + 1 = m-2`. Then `2*OD + 3 = 2m - 4 + 3 = 2m -1 = ID -1`. So `id0 + 6 = ID - 1 + 1 = ID`. Wait, compute: `id0 = (OD-1)*2 - 1 = (m-3)*2 - 1 = 2m - 7 = ID - 7`. Then `id0 + 6 = ID - 1`. This is `< ID`. Good. If `ID` is odd: `ID=2m+1`. `OD = floor((2m+1-5)/2)+1 = floor((2m-4)/2)+1 = (m-2)+1 = m-1`. Then `id0 = (m-2)*2 - 1 = 2m - 5 = ID - 6`. Then `id0 + 6 = ID`. Wait, `ID - 6 + 6 = ID`. That's exactly `ID`, which is out of bounds (valid indices 0..ID-1). Let's test: `ID=7`. `OD = floor((7-5)/2)+1 = 1+1=2`. `od=1`. `id0 = 1*2-1=1`. `id0+6=7`. `ID=7`. 7 >= 7. Out of bounds! For `kd=2`: `id=1+6=7`, which is invalid. But does this output even exist? Wait, for `ID=7`, `num=7+2-6-1=2`. `OD=2/2+1=2`. `od=0`: `id0=-1`. `od=1`: `id0=1`. For `kd=2`, `id=7`, which is >= 7, so invalid. But our fast path assumes `id0 >= 0` is enough. For `ID=7`, the fast path for `od=1` would access `id=7` which is out of bounds. So the specialized fast path is only safe when `ID` is large enough that `id0 + 6 < ID` for all valid `id0 >= 0`. Specifically, the smallest `ID` with non-zero output where this fails is `ID=7` (as shown). What about `ID=6`? `OD = floor((6-5)/2)+1 = 0+1=1`. Only `od=0`, `id0=-1`, fast path not taken. `ID=8`: `OD = floor(3/2)+1 = 1+1=2`. `od=1`, `id0=1`, `1+6=7 < 8`. Safe. `ID=9`: `OD = floor(4/2)+1=2+1=3`. `od=2`, `id0=3`, `3+6=9`. Out of bounds. So for odd `ID >= 9`, the fast path is unsafe. But the test uses `ID=128`. For the test, it's safe. For kw=0, iw = 2*ow - 1 (covers odd numbers: -1, 1, 3, 5, ...). For kw=1, iw = 2*ow + 2 (covers even numbers: 2, 4, 6, 8, ...). For kw=2, iw = 2*ow + 5 (covers odd numbers again: 5, 7, 9, ... which are covered by kw=0). Actually, kw=0 gives odd integers >= -1. kw=1 gives even integers >= 2. kw=1 misses 0? For ow=0, kw=1 gives 2. But can we get 0? iw = 2*ow - 1 + 3*kw = 0 => 2*ow + 3*kw = 1. This has no integer solution because 2*ow + 3*kw is always >= 0 for non-negative ow, kw. Actually, ow=-1 gives 2*(-1)+3*1 = 1, but ow=-1 is not in our range. So 0 is not accessible. And what about even negative numbers like -2? 2*ow -1 + 3*kw = -2 => 2*ow + 3*kw = -1. Impossible for ow>=0, kw>=0. So the set of accessible iw for a large range of ow is all integers in [min, max] except perhaps a few at the boundaries. For our block of ow in [0,31], union of iw is roughly [-1, 67], missing maybe a couple of values like 0. But effectively it's ~68 values. So a block of 32x8 output pixels reads from a region of about 3 (id) * ~20 (ih) * ~70 (iw) = ~4200 floats. This is about 4200 * 4 = 16.8 KB. This fits in shared memory (up to 227KB per block). 256 threads reading 4200 floats collectively means each thread reads about 16 floats to fill shared memory. That's a very small overhead. Then each thread does 27 reads from shared memory instead of global memory. Total global reads would drop from 6912 to ~420' (after accounting for the initial fill and that some values span across blocks, but there's overlap between adjacent blocks in the id dimension... actually, for a fixed od, id is fixed to 3 values. For adjacent oh blocks, the ih range shifts. There's little overlap in ih between adjacent blocks: block 0 covers ih approx [-1, 19], block 1 covers ih [15, 35] (since oh_start=8 gives ih0=15). Overlap is about 5 values. So not much reuse. But the major win is: global memory per output pixel drops from 27 reads to ~4200 / (32*8) = 16.4 reads per output pixel. That's a ~1.6x reduction! Shared memory bandwidth is ~13 TB/s on H100, much higher than the global bandwidth of 3.35 TB/s. This should give a nice speedup. However, implementing the shared memory tiling correctly with padding handling and dilation is complex, especially in a single kernel file. But the configuration is fixed (K=3, S=2, P=1, D=3). I can write a highly tuned kernel for this configuration. But given the complexity of writing a shared memory tile for 3D pooling with dilation and padding, and the time constraints, I should consider if there are simpler optimizations. Maybe thread coarsening along the 'od' (output depth) dimension? For a given (n,c,oh,ow), we could compute multiple od values. Each od value has different id0, so id values are id0, id0+3, id0+6. For consecutive od (say od=0 and od=1), id0 shifts by stride=2. So id0 for od=0 is -1, id0 for od=1 is 1. Accessed id for od=0: {-1, 2, 5}. For od=1: {1, 4, 7}. Union: {-1, 1, 2, 4, 5, 7}. No overlap in valid positive indices. But the ranges are close. If a thread handles 2 od values, it reads 2*3*3*3=54 values, but the id ranges might span ~8 values. Let me draft the specialized kernel with shared memory: ```cuda __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_k3s2p1d3_smem_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW) { __shared__ float smem[3][21][69]; int ow = blockIdx.x * 32 + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * 8 + threadIdx.y; int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; int id0 = od * 2 - 1; int block_oh_start = blockIdx.y * 8; int block_ow_start = blockIdx.x * 32; // Determine exact tile sizes for this block. // For IH: the needed span covers all possible global ih values for oh in [block_oh_start, min(block_oh_start+8, OH)-1] // The minimum ih accessed: int g_ih_min = block_oh_start * 2 - 1; // The maximum ih accessed: int oh_max_in_block = min(block_oh_start + 8, OH) - 1; int g_ih_max = oh_max_in_block * 2 - 1 + 6; // kh=2 -> +6 int ih_size = g_ih_max - g_ih_min + 1; // <= 21 int g_iw_min = block_ow_start * 2 - 1; int ow_max_in_block = min(block_ow_start + 32, OW) - 1; int g_iw_max = ow_max_in_block * 2 - 1 + 6; int iw_size = g_iw_max - g_iw_min + 1; // <= 69 int total_elements = 3 * ih_size * iw_size; int linear_tid = threadIdx.y * 32 + threadIdx.x; // Cooperative loading of the input tile into shared memory for (int e = linear_tid; e < total_elements; e += 256) { int d = e / (ih_size * iw_size); int rem = e % (ih_size * iw_size); int h = rem / iw_size; int w = rem % iw_size; int g_id = id0 + d * 3; int g_ih = g_ih_min + h; int g_iw = g_iw_min + w; float val = -FLT_MAX; if (g_id >= 0 && g_id < ID && g_ih >= 0 && g_ih < IH && g_iw >= 0 && g_iw < IW) { val = __ldg(input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * (size_t)ID * IH * IW + (size_t)g_id * IH * IW + (size_t)g_ih * IW + g_iw); } smem[d][h][w] = val; } __syncthreads(); if (ow < OW && oh < OH) { float maxval = -FLT_MAX; int smem_h_base = (oh - block_oh_start) * 2; int smem_w_base = (ow - block_ow_start) * 2; #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow; output[out_offset] = maxval; } } ``` Wait, there's a major bug: `smem` size is fixed at compile time to `[3][21][69]`. One crucial check: `__syncthreads()`. All threads in a block must reach it. The load loop is executed by all threads. After the loop, there is `__syncthreads()`. Drafting the final CUDA code: ```cuda #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cfloat> #include <cstdint> #include <algorithm> #include <torch/extension.h> __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_generic_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW, int K, int S, int P, int D) { int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y; int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return; int id0 = od * S - P; int ih0 = oh * S - P; int iw0 = ow * S - P; size_t plane = (size_t)ID * IH * IW; const float* in_ptr = input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * plane; float maxval = -FLT_MAX; #pragma unroll 1 for (int kd = 0; kd < K; ++kd) { int id = id0 + kd * D; if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue; size_t off_d = (size_t)id * IH * IW; #pragma unroll 1 for (int kh = 0; kh < K; ++kh) { int ih = ih0 + kh * D; if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue; size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)ih * IW; #pragma unroll 1 for (int kw = 0; kw < K; ++kw) { int iw = iw0 + kw * D; if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue; float val = __ldg(in_ptr + off_h + iw); if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow; output[out_offset] = maxval; } #define IH_TILE 21 #define IW_TILE 69 __global__ void maxpool3d_forward_k3s2p1d3_smem_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C, int ID, int IH, int IW, int OD, int OH, int OW) { __shared__ float smem[3][IH_TILE][IW_TILE]; int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y; int tmp = blockIdx.z; int od = tmp % OD; tmp /= OD; int c = tmp % C; int n = tmp / C; int id0 = od * 2 - 1; int block_oh_start = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y; int block_ow_start = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x; int oh_max_in_block = min(block_oh_start + blockDim.y, OH) - 1; int g_ih_min = block_oh_start * 2 - 1; int g_ih_max = oh_max_in_block * 2 - 1 + 6; int ih_size = g_ih_max - g_ih_min + 1; int ow_max_in_block = min(block_ow_start + blockDim.x, OW) - 1; int g_iw_min = block_ow_start * 2 - 1; int g_iw_max = ow_max_in_block * 2 - 1 + 6; int iw_size = g_iw_max - g_iw_min + 1; int total_elements = 3 * ih_size * iw_size; int linear_tid = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; size_t base_offset = ((size_t)n * C + c) * (size_t)ID * IH * IW; for (int e = linear_tid; e < total_elements; e += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int d = e / (ih_size * iw_size); int rem = e % (ih_size * iw_size); int h = rem / iw_size; int w = rem % iw_size; int g_id = id0 + d * 3; int g_ih = g_ih_min + h; int g_iw = g_iw_min + w; float val = -FLT_MAX; if (g_id >= 0 && g_id < ID && g_ih >= 0 && g_ih < IH && g_iw >= 0 && g_iw < IW) { val = __ldg(input + base_offset + (size_t)g_id * IH * IW + (size_t)g_ih * IW + g_iw); } smem[d][h][w] = val; } __syncthreads(); if (ow < OW && oh < OH) { float maxval = -FLT_MAX; int smem_h_base = (oh - block_oh_start) * 2; int smem_w_base = (ow - block_ow_start) * 2; #pragma unroll for (int kd = 0; kd < 3; ++kd) { #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < 3; ++kh) { int h = smem_h_base + kh * 3; #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < 3; ++kw) { int w = smem_w_base + kw * 3; float val = smem[kd][h][w]; if (val > maxval) maxval = val; } } } size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow; output[out_offset] = maxval; } } torch::Tensor maxpool3d_forward_cuda(...) { ... } ``` Wait, `blockDim.x` and `blockDim.y` are used to compute `linear_tid` and the stride. import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.nn.functional as F
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

cuda_source = r"""
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <cfloat>
#include <cstdint>
#include <algorithm>
#include <torch/extension.h>

__global__ void maxpool3d_forward_generic_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ input,
    float* __restrict__ output,
    int N, int C,
    int ID, int IH, int IW,
    int OD, int OH, int OW,
    int K, int S, int P, int D)
{
    int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x;
    int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y;

    int tmp = blockIdx.z;
    int od = tmp % OD;
    tmp /= OD;
    int c = tmp % C;
    int n = tmp / C;

    if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return;

    int id0 = od * S - P;
    int ih0 = oh * S - P;
    int iw0 = ow * S - P;

    size_t plane = (size_t)ID * IH * IW;
    const float* in_ptr = input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * plane;

    float maxval = -FLT_MAX;

    #pragma unroll 1
    for (int kd = 0; kd < K; ++kd) {
        int id = id0 + kd * D;
        if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue;
        size_t off_d = (size_t)id * IH * IW;
        #pragma unroll 1
        for (int kh = 0; kh < K; ++kh) {
            int ih = ih0 + kh * D;
            if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue;
            size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)ih * IW;
            #pragma unroll 1
            for (int kw = 0; kw < K; ++kw) {
                int iw = iw0 + kw * D;
                if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue;
                float val = __ldg(in_ptr + off_h + iw);
                if (val > maxval) maxval = val;
            }
        }
    }

    size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow;
    output[out_offset] = maxval;
}

__global__ void maxpool3d_forward_k3s2p1d3_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ input,
    float* __restrict__ output,
    int N, int C,
    int ID, int IH, int IW,
    int OD, int OH, int OW)
{
    int ow = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x;
    int oh = blockIdx.y * blockDim.y + threadIdx.y;

    int tmp = blockIdx.z;
    int od = tmp % OD;
    tmp /= OD;
    int c = tmp % C;
    int n = tmp / C;

    if (ow >= OW || oh >= OH) return;

    size_t plane = (size_t)ID * IH * IW;
    const float* in_ptr = input + ((size_t)n * C + c) * plane;

    int id0 = od * 2 - 1;
    int ih0 = oh * 2 - 1;
    int iw0 = ow * 2 - 1;

    float maxval = -FLT_MAX;

    bool fast = (id0 >= 0 && ih0 >= 0 && iw0 >= 0 &&
                 id0 + 6 < ID && ih0 + 6 < IH && iw0 + 6 < IW);

    if (fast) {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int kd = 0; kd < 3; ++kd) {
            size_t off_d = (size_t)(id0 + kd * 3) * IH * IW;
            #pragma unroll
            for (int kh = 0; kh < 3; ++kh) {
                size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)(ih0 + kh * 3) * IW;
                #pragma unroll
                for (int kw = 0; kw < 3; ++kw) {
                    float val = __ldg(in_ptr + off_h + iw0 + kw * 3);
                    if (val > maxval) maxval = val;
                }
            }
        }
    } else {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int kd = 0; kd < 3; ++kd) {
            int id = id0 + kd * 3;
            if (id < 0 || id >= ID) continue;
            size_t off_d = (size_t)id * IH * IW;
            #pragma unroll
            for (int kh = 0; kh < 3; ++kh) {
                int ih = ih0 + kh * 3;
                if (ih < 0 || ih >= IH) continue;
                size_t off_h = off_d + (size_t)ih * IW;
                #pragma unroll
                for (int kw = 0; kw < 3; ++kw) {
                    int iw = iw0 + kw * 3;
                    if (iw < 0 || iw >= IW) continue;
                    float val = __ldg(in_ptr + off_h + iw);
                    if (val > maxval) maxval = val;
                }
            }
        }
    }

    size_t out_offset = (size_t)blockIdx.z * OH * OW + (size_t)oh * OW + ow;
    output[out_offset] = maxval;
}

torch::Tensor maxpool3d_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor input,
                                     int kernel_size,
                                     int stride,
                                     int padding,
                                     int dilation,
                                     bool ceil_mode)
{
    auto x = input.contiguous();
    int N = x.size(0);
    int C = x.size(1);
    int ID = x.size(2);
    int IH = x.size(3);
    int IW = x.size(4);

    int K = kernel_size;
    int S = stride;
    if (S <= 0) S = K;
    int P = padding;
    int D = dilation;

    auto compute_out_size = [&](int64_t in_size) -> int64_t {
        int64_t num = in_size + 2 * P - D * (K - 1) - 1;
        return (num + (ceil_mode ? S - 1 : 0)) / S + 1;
    };

    int64_t OD = compute_out_size(ID);
    int64_t OH = compute_out_size(IH);
    int64_t OW = compute_out_size(IW);

    if (OD <= 0 || OH <= 0 || OW <= 0) {
        return torch::empty({N, C,
            std::max<int64_t>(OD, 0LL),
            std::max<int64_t>(OH, 0LL),
            std::max<int64_t>(OW, 0LL)}, x.options());
    }

    auto output = torch::empty({N, C, OD, OH, OW}, x.options());

    const int BX = 32;
    const int BY = 8;
    dim3 block(BX, BY, 1);
    dim3 grid(
        (OW + BX - 1) / BX,
        (OH + BY - 1) / BY,
        N * C * OD
    );

    bool is_specialized = (K == 3 && S == 2 && P == 1 && D == 3 && !ceil_mode);

    if (is_specialized) {
        maxpool3d_forward_k3s2p1d3_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(
            x.data_ptr<float>(),
            output.data_ptr<float>(),
            N, C,
            ID, IH, IW,
            OD, OH, OW
        );
    } else {
        maxpool3d_forward_generic_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(
            x.data_ptr<float>(),
            output.data_ptr<float>(),
            N, C,
            ID, IH, IW,
            OD, OH, OW,
            K, S, P, D
        );
    }

    cudaError_t err = cudaGetLastError();
    if (err != cudaSuccess) {
        TORCH_CHECK(false, "maxpool3d_forward_cuda kernel launch failed: ", cudaGetErrorString(err));
    }
    return output;
}
"""

cpp_source = r"""
#include <torch/extension.h>
torch::Tensor maxpool3d_forward_cuda(torch::Tensor input, int kernel_size, int stride, int padding, int dilation, bool ceil_mode);
"""

_maxpool3d_ext = load_inline(
    name="maxpool3d_cuda",
    cpp_sources=cpp_source,
    cuda_sources=cuda_source,
    functions=["maxpool3d_forward_cuda"],
    extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"],
    verbose=False,
)

class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, kernel_size, stride=None, padding=0, dilation=1, return_indices=False, ceil_mode=False):
        super(ModelNew, self).__init__()
        self.kernel_size = kernel_size
        self.stride = stride if stride is not None else kernel_size
        self.padding = padding
        self.dilation = dilation
        self.return_indices = return_indices
        self.ceil_mode = ceil_mode

    def forward(self, x):
        if self.return_indices:
            return F.max_pool3d(
                x, self.kernel_size, self.stride,
                self.padding, self.dilation,
                self.ceil_mode, self.return_indices
            )
        return _maxpool3d_ext.maxpool3d_forward_cuda(
            x,
            self.kernel_size,
            self.stride,
            self.padding,
            self.dilation,
            self.ceil_mode,
        )
